I would have given them five stars if it wasn't for the fact that every other time I stop by I cannot get anyone to help me.  I have no idea how anyone can pick a putter out.  Really they have hundreds to choose and even more if you don't need a new one.  Geez!   In the past year I have bought three entire sets of clubs here none of which were for me.  Wife one and two for work colleges that won them.   This place is near an auction that I attend several times per month so I stop by each time.  Each visit is worth a couple of hundred bucks.  I have my eye on the USC cart bag they have now.  We will see.
Also the selection of gloves is pretty good.  They crew there is very nice and they have a place you can swing at a computer screen and test clubs.
The employees act as if they know what they are talking about not that I would know my golf game blows and no matter what clubs I get I'm not sure it will blow any less.  I think the manager is a stick I can tell by the way he rolls his eyes when I take a swat at the ball in the simulator.
Anyway fun place to go, prices are fair (from what I can tell), you can't make a mistake one day that you cannot undo the next so there is some peace of mind with that.  Meaning they take anything back even if used.  Albeit for credit toward other items.  If you need any golf stuff you'd be crazy not to try this place.< /text>

<Text>The San Francisco Police Department is AWESOME!!!!!!! My 19 year old daughter got on a bus in Harrison, Arkansas Tuesday San Francisco bound - she was supposed to arrive in San Francisco today at 6:30 p.m. I hadn't heard from her in hours so I called the San Francisco Police Department. They had an officer go to the Greyhound bus station to check to see if my daughter got off of the bus when it arrived there at 6:30 p.m. and she hadn't. I then heard from Officer Pena-Dega. He was real thorough with the questions he asked me about my daughter - he even asked for recent pictures of her and then he called me back and said they were going to have an officer check things out in Reno, Nevada too. He told me to call if I heard from my daughter. I FINALLY heard from my daughter - she wasn't on the bus that had arrived in San Francisco at 6:30 - she was on a different bus and the weather was bad - she couldn't charge her phone - she said they were in Sacramento and would be in San Francisco in 2 hours. I called the San Francisco Police Department back to let them know and Officer Pena-Dega called me back and asked me if I would still like for him to go by the Greyhound bus station to check to see if my daughter made it - I told him that would be great if possible - he said he would if he was able to and he did! He even let my daughter call me on his cell phone and he even helped my daughter find a shelter to stay in - he was a God send! :) I am REALLY pleased with the San Francisco Police Department - all police departments should be like them - they were very nice, courteous, and respectful of me and they took this situation seriously instead of telling me there was nothing they could do. < review>
Mark was great. Easy to talk to, professional in every way.

I do have an issue with the administration's dispatching strategy:

In the first call on 8/24, you sent a technician with a camera to make a prognosis, but no tools to fix.

In the second call on 8/30, you did the opposite: you sent a technician to fix the problem, but no camera to troubleshoot.

This management dysfunction has an industry label: "efficient but not effective".

The result: The client's problem still isn't fixed. The technicians still don't know why. The customer (me) has cancelled his own work hours for a total 4 days (2 of those days, the appointments were cancelled by Ben Franklin).

I would suggest future visits bring 1) the tools to fix, 2) a camera to troubleshoot... and 3) the original technicians, as new technicians suffer from inevitable loss in knowledge transfer.

I gave 3 stars for:

- Courteousness of call center reps
- Ben Franklin's tardy policy
- Professional, competent technicians (who suffer from ineffective management strategies, see above).<//review>

<rate>5<//rate><text>We have a detached, 100 sq. ft. finished studio in our backyard, up an inclined slope that had no plumbing whatsoever. We've been renting it on Airbnb, and recently decided to add a toilet and sink. This proved to be quite the challenging project! I got several quotes, and most plumbers didn't know how to handle the access, trenching lines, and other technical issues. Some wanted me to hire day laborers to do the digging, a prospect that I was uncomfortable with, not knowing how to direct them to properly dig the trenches, and worried about damaging things. Skyler came out and basically solved all our problems with one planning visit. Even better, he confidently explained how they would handle the process from start to finish, including all the digging, pipe work, and trimming out. Furthermore, their being fully insured was important to me. He even recommended a rear discharge toilet, something that no one else had mentioned. This allowed the toilet installation to happen without major dirt excavation of the sloped ground beneath the  studio. A big win!

Every single day of this five day project, workers arrived on time, worked efficiently and diligently, and cleaned up nicely. The men who did the trench work and concrete cutting and finishing (Pasang and Ming) were knowledgable and articulate, and I found out that they were Sherpas, actually leading expeditions up Mt. Everest! Amazing stamina! Ben Franklin is very lucky to have these guys on their team.

Skyler and his associate Justin oversaw the major elements of the job, and were a pleasure to deal with. Skyler even expertly deflected questions from our nosey neighbors who have been continuously harassing us for the past year about our personal business. We are thrilled to have a difficult project finished, and one that involved such creativity. < Review>
The Ambrose Butchery is not half as cool and swanky as they think they are. They do things like have a tiny menu printed on a single sheet of paper as though they have dishes that changed frequently, but the offerings they had were the same as the ones on their website. (It doesn't change either.)

They have 3 non alcoholic beverages and none of them were things like iced tea or soda. The Butchery is very alcohol centric which doesn't suit me, or a lot of people other people too.

Similarly to the menu, I've seen this done in actually fancy places and have it work, but not with burgers and fried chicken sandwiches that weren't exceptional, it seems like an affectation.

There are more refined items than those on their menu that I didn't try so that might be a slight overreaction. But I just got back from there and it put me in a bad mood.

Part of the reason that's true is because we had to wait 35 minutes, standing around outside, at  6pm on a normal Wednesday evening. I figured it had to be good.

However, I wouldn't recommend it. They play cool music and have groovy stickers though.<//Review>

The ingredients are fresh and premium. The servings are enough to get full, and still have enough to take home. The ambiance is fun and presented in a clean aesthetic with tasteful rock/ punk vibe. The financial investment is evident, but what sets this place apart from anywhere else within a 12 mile radius is the food preparation. It's part of my top five East Bay list.</Text>

<user_id>114714540192669718999<//user_id>< name>
B. Li<//name>
<Time>1569847365636< /Time><Rate>4</Rate>< review>
Great new local butchery and restaurant in the Niles district. You'll find it on the main Niles road just a few feet from Mantiques.

Ordered their chips and dip, bacon mac & cheese, and burger.

They try to do everything in-house and there's definitely a lot of high notes and some points on improvement.

The onion dip is delicious, no complaints here, just need to be a bit careful as the chips are thin and break easily.

Mac and cheese was a great appetizer to share. The bacon had a smokiness to it and was thick enough where it had a little give while still being crispy. The gruyere cheese mellowed the savoriness of the bacon, but the macaroni had a bit of doughiness to it. Not quite as smooth a texture as I prefer, but not enough to mar the dish.

The burger has great ingredients behind it. A bun that stays firm and holds the contents together. Pickles that are crisp and have that satisfying crunch. Mustard seeds that add some spice to the burger. A juicy beef patty that's been rested properly so it's not dripping out all its flavors.

The only thing that could've improved the burger was more seasoning. The tomato jam was good, but might've made the burger taste more sweet than savory. Maybe some smoked paprika or a sauce to boost it's savoriness.

Last thing to note is that the butchery is not open on Sundays. Also, dinner has a separate menu with some great looking choices. Will probably visit here again to try their tri-tip.</review>

< name>
Bruce MacNaughton<//name>
< Time>
1572719602841<//Time>
<rating>5</rating>< review>
The best American restaurant in Fremont, hands down. Ambrose Butchery has a small menu, big portions (maybe a bit too big), and very high quality food and people.

It's a charming butcher shop-restaurant combination, though the butcher shop is very limited, even more so than the menu. I went for lunch the first time and had the burger. It was made with tomato jam instead of tomatoes and had shredded lettuce (not the little pieces that fall out when you try to eat the sandwich, but long intertwined strands that give a unique texture), and wonderful meat. It's good and worth going for. I've also tried the sausage sandwich - piping hot onions and peppers with a beautifully flavored sausage work together perfectly. I'm trying the Reuben next.

I've been to dinner as well - the breakfast brie appetizer is wonderful, as is the mac & cheese (be forewarned - the portion is enough that it needs to be split between 3-4 people, or just order the mac & cheese as an entree - it's rich). I had the seared duck breast - nicely done rare pan seared duck breast with kabocha squash and rapini. My wife had the oxtail with pickled onions on collard greens.

And they serve DasBrew, local German-style beers, among other fine selections like Dogfish Head. Oh, and Fentiman's soft drinks.

The place is special. So special I'm torn about writing a good review for them because I don't want them to be too crowded or grow too big. But I want that for them, so I'm not being selfish.</review>

Great burgers, especially if you‚Äôre into something more traditional! I got a cheeseburger and fries, with an iced tea and a whole chocolate cream pie for under $30. Pretty great pricing!

< review>
Some of the best pie you'll find around.  The food is made to order to go or eat in and the pie is a great addition to your dinner if you've eaten somewhere else already.  The price for a whole pie varies on the type you get, but well worth it.  They have the main staples of pies and seasonal ones as well.  If you want to share something tasty with someone you care about, and they like pie(my wifes doesn't sadly) bring them here or stop on your way home and get some.  They sell by slice, half, and whole pie for sure.</review>

<review>Cool little burger joint. We were coming home from a late pickup at Oakland airport and we were looking for a late night place to get the kids a treat for a being so good on the drive down.

This place was recommend by another restaurant we stopped at that did not serve milkshakes. When we walked in the kids were excited to see a whole display or pies and treats. It was busy, even though it was late night, so the food took a long time to come out. But they quickly brought us our pies so the kids would be occuPIEd while we waited (pun inttended).

The sweets were great, and the milkshakes were delicious. Burgers were good too, but not exceptional.

My only complaint is that there was a large number of homeless/ vagrants in and around the establishment, which is always expected in Oakland and SF. But for some reason this place let's them mingle inside the restaurant. So that was a little bit scary with the kids running around. My kids are well versed in inner city travels, so they interacted fine with the many vagrants around. But if your family isn't used to it, maybe find another spot if it's late at night.</review><Pics>None</Pics>< response>
